  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_45fb76a1-5099-4824-9621-1f9a3863a78c'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText18339693065364578844" style="display:none">Luna is a no-hoper with a secret: in a world of illusion, she can see what is real. But can she see the truth before it is too late? <br /> <br />Luna has always been able to exist in virtual and real worlds at the same time, a secret she is warned to keep. She hides her ability by being a Refuser: excluded by choice from the virtual spheres others inhabit. But when she is singled out for testing, she can’t hide any longer. <br /> <br />The safest thing to do would be to fail, to go back to a dead-end life, no future. But Luna is starting to hope for something better, and hope is a dangerous thing...</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1128506302?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1128506302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3367214813187936874">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to Hachette Children's Books and NetGalley.)<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Don’t let them notice you’re different.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428054705i/14355468.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was an interesting sci-fi/dystopian story, and I loved the twists.<br/><br/>I felt quite sorry for Luna at the start of this story. The way everyone treated her like a second-class citizen because she didn’t want to ‘plug-in’ to the virtual world was pretty bad. Especially considering that she hadn’t spoken to her father in</span>
  <span id="freeText3367214813187936874" style="display:none">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to Hachette Children's Books and NetGalley.)<br><br><b>
  <i>“Don’t let them notice you’re different.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428054705i/14355468.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was an interesting sci-fi/dystopian story, and I loved the twists.<br><br>I felt quite sorry for Luna at the start of this story. The way everyone treated her like a second-class citizen because she didn’t want to ‘plug-in’ to the virtual world was pretty bad. Especially considering that she hadn’t spoken to her father in weeks because he chose to be plugged-in all the time, and never came back to his body to see her.<br><br><b>
  <i>“What were you thinking?” she says. “I’ve a good mind to get your father in here, and –”<br>I look up. I know an empty threat when I hear one. “Please do. I haven’t seen him in weeks.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428054705i/14355469.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The storyline in this followed Luna as her plans to get expelled backfired, and she found herself being given the sort of assignment that she really didn’t want. There were so many twists in this story though! The pace itself was very slow in places, but thankfully the twists made up for it, especially the ones at the end. I also liked how the author managed to work her previous book ‘Slated’ into the storyline of this one!<br><br><b>
  <i>“What is this fictional world, ‘Slated’? I’ve never heard of it,” I say out loud.</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1322670665l/12743472.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There wasn’t really any romance in this one, other than Luna stating categorically that she was not going to have a relationship with her best friend’s boyfriend, just because they were in the same place together.<br><br><br>The ending to this had lots of twists, and it was these that definitely bumped up the rating on this one for me. The slowness of this story made it a three, but the twists made it a 4.<br><br><b>
  <i>“When I finally turn and meet their eyes I smile for the first time in a long while. I may seek the truth, but I still have my secrets.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428054705i/14355470._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>7.5 out of 10<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3367214813187936874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7269805377631425907" style="display:none"><b>5 Words: Family, love, virtual, conspiracy, control.</b><br /><br />My mind is blown. I am now an empty shell of my former self. It may take a while for me to recover. So you'll have to come back later for my actual review.<br /><br />Ok, so I'm back.<br /><br />And this book was pretty awesome.<br /><br />I got so caught up in the story. It just flowed so well and had such an incredible pace. It was supposed to be a 5-chapters-a-day buddy read, but we both pretty much raced through it.<br /><br />Mind Games is set in a pretty twisted world, and I loved the conspiracy, the idea of free-choice and yet everyone being controlled or pressurised.<br /><br />There is a hint of romance in the story, but it never over-takes the rest of the plot. It's just pretty natural feelings growing as two people spend time together.<br /><br />And that ending was crushing.<br /><br /><i>I received a copy of this for free via NetGalley for review purposes.</i></span>

<div id="review_1166022157" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1166022157" />
    <a title="Nicola" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8803703-nicola"><img alt="Nicola" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587222161p2/8803703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1166022157?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicola" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicola" href="/user/show/8803703-nicola">Nicola</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24555478-mind-games">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8803703-nicola?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1166022157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15582342948325560525">Luna lives in a world where the majority of the population has an implant allowing them access to a virtual world. Everyone learns, lives, plays and interacts in this virtual world. Luna is one of few “Refusers”, who choose not to have an implant and do things the old way, like learn in a physical classroom with physical teachers. When she does enter the virtual world, we discover that she has a dangerous secret: she is aware of both the virtual world <b>and</b> the real world around her.<br/><br/>This book remi</span>
  <span id="freeText15582342948325560525" style="display:none">Luna lives in a world where the majority of the population has an implant allowing them access to a virtual world. Everyone learns, lives, plays and interacts in this virtual world. Luna is one of few “Refusers”, who choose not to have an implant and do things the old way, like learn in a physical classroom with physical teachers. When she does enter the virtual world, we discover that she has a dangerous secret: she is aware of both the virtual world <b>and</b> the real world around her.<br /><br />This book reminded me of a few others due to similarities in the story. The fact Luna has a dangerous secret that she can’t tell anyone else, for fear of the PareCo corporation finding out and controlling her, is like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13335037.Divergent__Divergent___1_" title="Divergent (Divergent, #1) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Divergent</a>. The most promising teenagers in schools being chosen to take part in tests to establish where they belong in society is like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13326831.The_Testing__The_Testing___1_" title="The Testing (The Testing, #1) by Joelle Charbonneau" rel="nofollow noopener">The Testing</a>. The implant technology and how everyone in society chooses, and prefers, to interact virtually rather than in reality, is like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20642438.Glaze" title="Glaze by Kim Curran" rel="nofollow noopener">Glaze</a>. I really enjoyed elements from all of these novels being brought together in Mind Games. <br /><br />I liked the writing. I think it flowed really well. I also enjoyed the world building and I was able to really picture the world that Luna was living in. One small gripe I had is that Luna doesn’t really have any flaws. She can quickly learn how to do things that have taken other hackers years to master. There isn’t anything that she can’t do. This is somewhat explained by the fact she was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[genetically engineered <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but it was a little tiresome at times. <br /><br />The idea of the implant technology is creepy because it’s really not hard to imagine that it could happen in <b>our</b> society in the future. The thought of being able to attend school whilst actually chilling at home in pyjamas, being able to alter how you look, visit different worlds, it all sounds great, right? Considering the speed at which technology advances nowadays, it’s not difficult to envision a future with this kind of technology. The thought of a corporation like PareCo controlling and tracking us is what makes it scary. <br /><br />If you like YA dystopian fiction and you liked Divergent then this is a must-read book for you.<br /><br /><i>I received a copy of this book from the publishers via NetGalley.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15582342948325560525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="gio" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23204207-gio"><img alt="gio" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597613414p2/23204207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1229251954?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="gio" class="user" itemprop="url" name="gio" href="/user/show/23204207-gio">gio</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23204207-gio?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1229251954" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2136302367613524175"><i>*I received an ebook copy of this book through Netgalley in exchange for an honest review</i>*<br/><br/>Mind games has a quite interesting premise. Luna is a Refuser, a girl who refuses to plug into the virtual world in which most people spend their life now. By doing this <br/>she has become a social pariah and has little hopes for her future. Suddenly one day she's given a chance, a test that will define her future. <br/><br/>The plot is really similar to other dystopian books. At first I was quite enjoying reading Mind g</span>
  <span id="freeText2136302367613524175" style="display:none"><i>*I received an ebook copy of this book through Netgalley in exchange for an honest review</i>*<br /><br />Mind games has a quite interesting premise. Luna is a Refuser, a girl who refuses to plug into the virtual world in which most people spend their life now. By doing this <br />she has become a social pariah and has little hopes for her future. Suddenly one day she's given a chance, a test that will define her future. <br /><br />The plot is really similar to other dystopian books. At first I was quite enjoying reading Mind games to be honest, even if it wasn't the most original read, it was quite entertaining. However at some point I started noticing all its flaws. <br /><br />The world-building is poorly done in my opinion. We are thrown into this world but we never receive an explanation as on why things are this way, why people live in this virtual world and this was a disappointment. <br /><br />The characters were extremely flat and their relationship were quite ridiculous. I mean, Luna falls for a boy three days after she met him. The secondary characters are quite stereotypical.<br /><br />After the first half things started to go downhill fast. The plot didn't make much sense anymore and the pace of the book became so fast that it wasn't even that easy to follow the story.<br /><br />The ending didn't make much sense honestly.<br /><br />Mind games had a good premise but in my opinion the book as a whole didn't live up to it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2136302367613524175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText11032120284458824019" style="display:none">Luna is an outcast, identifying as a Refuser, someone who doesn't plug into the virtual world that surrounds her. <div id="review_1232744247" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1232744247" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2917700-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483254339p2/2917700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1232744247?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/2917700-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2917700-rebecca?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2917700-rebecca?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2917700-rebecca?shelf=genre-sci-fi">genre-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1232744247" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6697325988598657798"><i>I received a copy of this book from the publishers via NetGalley.</i><br/><br/>Think of Mind Games as a blend of Divergent meets Ready Player One meets Corruption.<br/><br/>It’s some time in the distant future and the vast majority of the world’s population is plugged into a virtual world. The few that aren’t are considered “Refusers”, most of which are Medical Exemption as they have a medical condition that disqualifies them from being able to use the technology, or Religious Exemptions because of their religion (duh)</span>
  <span id="freeText6697325988598657798" style="display:none"><i>I received a copy of this book from the publishers via NetGalley.</i><br /><br />Think of Mind Games as a blend of Divergent meets Ready Player One meets Corruption.<br /><br />It’s some time in the distant future and the vast majority of the world’s population is plugged into a virtual world. The few that aren’t are considered “Refusers”, most of which are Medical Exemption as they have a medical condition that disqualifies them from being able to use the technology, or Religious Exemptions because of their religion (duh). Our MFC Luna is neither of these, yet she still Refuses to use the tech, making life very difficult for her. As a small child, when she would plug in to the virtual world, she would get debilitatingly nauseas. Not only that, but something else happens - something she is determined to keep secret.<br /><br />As a result, she goes through life trying to be mediocre, despite her intelligence. She aims to keep to the bottom of the pack so that she doesn’t get picked for a special exam at the end of her schooling which would ultimately end in a prized internship with PareCor - the company in charge of this whole virtual reality. The jokes on her though when she gets an invitation anyway. <br /><br />The plot was gripping and super intriguing, yet sometimes I kept getting pulled out of the story. Mostly this had to do with the fact that I’m <i>still</i> not clear on what this whole virtual thing is. Like, what is it that goes into these games that allows someone to die in real life? Is it your consciousness? I’m still not clear on that and it kept pissing me off. I couldn’t figure out the connection between the body and this virtual reality, and it made it hard for me to enjoy and even understand certain bits of the storyline. That being said, what I could understand was fabulous.<br /><br />Luna, named after my beloved Luna Lovegood (for real), is a pretty cool character, yet a little passive at times. I felt like throughout most of the book she just let things happen instead of actively trying to do things. It took a while but she did get there in the end. Oh yes, and she’s a “special snowflake” and is actually described as being special a couple times throughout the book <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[if only because of the whole ‘genetic engineering’ angle which could’ve been so great if expanded upon a little more <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />Some of the secondary characters were awesome as well. I thought Marina was a fantastic character and would’ve loved to get to know her better, as well as Rachel and Melrose. Gecko was interesting and so was Hex. Unfortunately, I feel as though these characters weren’t really well rounded enough. Even the “villain” of this book, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[i.e. Tempo <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, felt kind of one dimensional.<br /><br />Overall, while the storyline was interesting and I really liked the concept, I was confused for a fair bit of the book. I feel like the story could have benefitted with a little more world-building and a better thought out ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6697325988598657798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1130559478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1130559478" />
    <a title="Aurélie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14667009-aur-lie"><img alt="Aurélie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604593947p2/14667009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1130559478?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aurélie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aurélie" href="/user/show/14667009-aur-lie">Aurélie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14667009-aur-lie?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1130559478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10364747642597212086">More reviews on my blog, <a href='http://exploringpages.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Exploring Pages</a>.<br/><blockquote><i>"Five minutes of Realtime, and it is nearly two hours before I stop being sick. That's a pretty good reason to be a Refuser, isn't it?"</i><br/>― Teri Terry, <i>Mind Games</i></blockquote><br/><br/><b>Thank you Orchard Books for providing me with an advanced reading copy for review.<br/><br/>DNF at 50 %</b><br/><br/>I wonder if I was fooled by the gorgeous cover, or the premise of <i>Mind Games</i>. As with so many books these days, a synopsis can be either exactly what you think it is, or turn out to be something entirely dif</span>
  <span id="freeText10364747642597212086" style="display:none">More reviews on my blog, <a href="http://exploringpages.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Exploring Pages</a>.<br /><blockquote><i>"Five minutes of Realtime, and it is nearly two hours before I stop being sick. That's a pretty good reason to be a Refuser, isn't it?"</i><br />― Teri Terry, <i>Mind Games</i></blockquote><br /><br /><b>Thank you Orchard Books for providing me with an advanced reading copy for review.<br /><br />DNF at 50 %</b><br /><br />I wonder if I was fooled by the gorgeous cover, or the premise of <i>Mind Games</i>. As with so many books these days, a synopsis can be either exactly what you think it is, or turn out to be something entirely different. It's sad to say that Teri Terry's novel falls into the last category.<br /><br />Throughout my reading experience, it was required to read this book with all the attention and focus I could get. Most of the times it's not necessarily a bad thing, but I didn't like how <i>Mind Games</i> played with my mind. I had to read every single word with care and attention, in order to follow along and understand both the story and the world building. Nonetheless, I still got very confused along the way. Mind you, I don't hold a single grudge against being thrown into the world of a book without any explanations. It's mostly a lot of fun because I have to figure out what is going on all on my own, but not in this case.<br /><br />There was an overload of unknown terms, combined with such little explanation. The only choice I had was to continue anyway and hope that I would be less confused as I go on. None of that happened. Once I started to get a hold of the story, so many other aspects turned my knowledge into chaos. A lot of that had to do with Terry's futuristic world full of technology. This is where a certain aspect I adored jumps in: the virtual reality. It was my ultimate main reason for requesting the book in the first place, and also what made the book so fascinating. It was so different from any other dystopian I've read before. How could I not be excited about that? However, things started to take a turn when I that aspect fell flat. In my opinion, there wasn't much world building to be found. I felt like a lot was just thrown in my face, and I had to deal with it. I couldn't connect to anything and because of the lack of world building, I never understood how it all worked or how some things were even possible.<br /><br />The vague plot dragged immensely, and at some point I had no desire whatsoever in picking it up again, ultimately resulting in a DNF. As sad as I am to admit it, <i>Mind Games</i> was all in all, a boring read which could have been so much more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10364747642597212086" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1190551476" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1190551476" />
    <a title="Kate Ormand" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7481046-kate-ormand"><img alt="Kate Ormand" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530872651p2/7481046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1190551476?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate Ormand" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate Ormand" href="/user/show/7481046-kate-ormand">Kate Ormand</a>

          added it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1190551476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15948489992788819374">This was like nothing I've read before, set in a high-tech world where most living is done in virtual realities. People take virtual vacations, go to school virtually, have virtual relationships. Luna is a Refuser -- she rejects an implant because when she enters the virtual worlds, she can still sense the body she leaves behind, and the connection makes her sick. Her nanna warns her of the dangers, never to tell anyone, but doesn't give away much more, meaning once Luna finds a way to overcome </span>
  <span id="freeText15948489992788819374" style="display:none">This was like nothing I've read before, set in a high-tech world where most living is done in virtual realities. People take virtual vacations, go to school virtually, have virtual relationships. Luna is a Refuser -- she rejects an implant because when she enters the virtual worlds, she can still sense the body she leaves behind, and the connection makes her sick. Her nanna warns her of the dangers, never to tell anyone, but doesn't give away much more, meaning once Luna finds a way to overcome her nausea, the virtual world is her oyster. <br /><br />If there's one thing I know I'll get from a book by Teri Terry it's genius world-building, and this delivered on that as much as the Slated trilogy. We see multiple virtual spaces, a closed-off mysterious island, and a futuristic real world, all incredibly well shaped. The story takes surprising turns that racks up the tension from start to finish, and the questions pile up to an exciting conclusion. What is PareCo, and what really goes on on Inaccessible Island? Play their game and find out... </span>
  <a data-text-id="15948489992788819374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer459571526571333314">I received a copy of this in exchange for review from netgalley, thanks! <br/><br/>Mind Games was a really interesting sci-fi/dystopian book, it took me a little while to get into it but in the end I definitely enjoyed it. I liked Luna, her refusal to get the implant for the virtual worlds was intriguing. I really felt sorry for her at times though, her mother is dead, her step mum doesn't really seem all that bothered, her dad is constantly 'plugged in' to the virtual world, and her nanna is dying. Its a</span>
  <span id="freeText459571526571333314" style="display:none">I received a copy of this in exchange for review from netgalley, thanks! <br /><br />Mind Games was a really interesting sci-fi/dystopian book, it took me a little while to get into it but in the end I definitely enjoyed it. I liked Luna, her refusal to get the implant for the virtual worlds was intriguing. I really felt sorry for her at times though, her mother is dead, her step mum doesn't really seem all that bothered, her dad is constantly 'plugged in' to the virtual world, and her nanna is dying. Its all a bit tough for her. <br /><br />I liked the idea of the virtual worlds and the hacking, it was a little complicated and confusing at times but still interesting. The book was a bit slow in parts but I thought the big twists made up for that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ omg the brains!!!! Who takes brains out of heads and puts them in tanks!! AND then Gecko was all like yeah I don't think you can unplug me all casual! AND Hex wanted that?! That part was just mental!! The story just didn't go how I expected it to at all. I thought there would be a big romance between Luna and Gecko but he spends a lot of time as a BRAIN IN A JAR!! I really don't think I an get past that!!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Definitely an interesting read! </span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1217427470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14848821803769689681">I was sent a copy of this book from Hatchette Children's Books, via NetGalley, in exchange for an honest review. First thing's first, I absolutely love the cover of this book, it's beautiful. It also has a rather 1984-esque feel to it, which I'm not sure is intentional but, given what the book is about, it wouldn't surprise me.<br/><br/>Although nothing like it in terms of plot, I also definitely had a bit of a reminder of Ready Player One when I read this. Mostly because of the virtual reality world that</span>
  <span id="freeText14848821803769689681" style="display:none">I was sent a copy of this book from Hatchette Children's Books, via NetGalley, in exchange for an honest review. First thing's first, I absolutely love the cover of this book, it's beautiful. It also has a rather 1984-esque feel to it, which I'm not sure is intentional but, given what the book is about, it wouldn't surprise me.<br /><br />Although nothing like it in terms of plot, I also definitely had a bit of a reminder of Ready Player One when I read this. Mostly because of the virtual reality world that existed and the way it was structured. However, this was a much darker and more dystopian storyline. Enough comparisons though, this book was so utterly unique and incredible that it doesn't need them! I love that it was set (mostly) in a futuristic England, something you don't normally see, and also that it didn't seem typically dystopian at first. In fact, it almost felt like maybe the future could be like this.<br /><br />The characters were all brilliant, funny and felt so real. I really liked the main character in this; I felt she was very strong yet very naive which worked perfectly in the book. I also loved Gecko and Hex and all the other Hackers. (But especially Gecko) I thought the idea of the Hackers were such an interesting concept and also the way PareCo worked to let them see what they could do. The characters all felt so three-dimensional (absolutely all of them) and I loved the exploration into the virtual world. It was such a unique idea the way it worked and how it affected different people.<br /><br />Also, I love stand-alone books. There just isn't enough of them in Young Adult literature these days, in my opinion; so it's great to find a stand-alone that manages to fulfil everything I'd usually expect from a series. This book had so much mystery and intrigue in it. It is partly a thriller and you definitely get that feeling when reading it.<br /><br />And THE TWISTS! (Yes, plural)! They were brilliant! And I genuinely didn't see the last one coming at all. It was so dark yet so intriguing and I absolutely loved it. Although I own Slated by Teri Terry I've not actually got around to reading it yet but I certainly will be now, especially after the inclusion of her own book in this, which I loved. An entire world about her own book: genius!<br /><br />I absolutely recommend this to anyone who enjoys Dystopian fiction and is a bit bored of the same-old young adult dystopians going around, because this is so so different. Also if anyone out there is a fan of thrillers, Ready Player One or 1984 then this is most certainly a book for you. I will definitely be picking up a physical copy as soon as I can because I'll be giving it a re-read soon. (Also, like I said before, that's a beautiful cover and I need it on my bookshelf). Thank you Teri Terry for writing such a brilliant book.<br /><br />To see this review and more on my blog, you can click here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://sarahthomasbooks.blogspot.com/2015/03/book-review-mind-games-by-teri-terry.html">http://sarahthomasbooks.blogspot.com/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14848821803769689681" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1157172008" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1157172008" />
    <a title="Maddie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18523225-maddie"><img alt="Maddie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531656548p2/18523225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1157172008?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddie" href="/user/show/18523225-maddie">Maddie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18523225-maddie?shelf=ukya">ukya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18523225-maddie?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1157172008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4090270633282708395">Originally at <a href='http://heartfullofbooks.com/2015/01/20/review-mind-games-by-teri-terry/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heart Full Of Books</a> <br/><br/>If I was going to compare this book to any other, it would be Fearsome Dreamer by Laure Eve, because of the similarities in world-building. So, if you like your fantasy books to have a more technological feel, then this is the book for you. And if you’re read Slated by Teri Terry, you’ll be able to recognise similarities between the main characters.<br/><br/>‘Mind Games’ is all about a girl called Luna, (a name that seems to be so linked to Harry Potter, you have to basic</span>
  <span id="freeText4090270633282708395" style="display:none">Originally at <a href="http://heartfullofbooks.com/2015/01/20/review-mind-games-by-teri-terry/" rel="nofollow noopener">Heart Full Of Books</a> <br /><br />If I was going to compare this book to any other, it would be Fearsome Dreamer by Laure Eve, because of the similarities in world-building. So, if you like your fantasy books to have a more technological feel, then this is the book for you. And if you’re read Slated by Teri Terry, you’ll be able to recognise similarities between the main characters.<br /><br />‘Mind Games’ is all about a girl called Luna, (a name that seems to be so linked to Harry Potter, you have to basically credit J.K.Rowling to use it) and her life in a world that’s slowly becoming consumed by technology. Luna is a ‘Rejector’, meaning that she doesn’t participate in the technological universe via implant. There is lots of terminology throughout this book to do with the world, so hold tight.<br /><br />Luna is especially gifted, however, in the techno-universe, despite refusing to go there. So, she’s recruited by the government figures, Pare-Co, to come for testing and eventually to work for them. She find out that her gift has a name and it turns out her skills were inherited from her mother.<br /><br />Although this book falls heavily into the fantasy genre, I thought that the world building was slightly lacking. I lost myself at the beginning, trying to navigate around all this terminology and the purpose of the implants. However, once the plot progressed and we learnt about Luna’s powers, I found a clearer direction. So many different things happened in ‘Mind Games’, it felt 1000 pages long.<br /><br />That’s not to say I didn’t absolutely love what was going on. Because of the intense variety of action, I couldn’t put the book down. I had to know what happened next as I couldn’t guess! I really enjoyed the romance aspect of the book, but was disappointed at the disappearance of Gecko, the love interest, for quite a long period of time. He and Luna did reunite, but Gecko was a really great character, and I missed him.<br /><br />When Luna was taken to the training island, some freaky stuff started to happen. The plot can only be compared to ‘Wreck-It Ralph’, when Ralph is jumping between video games. It was kind of like Luna was moving through a mind palace of settings, even the setting from Teri Terry’s previous series, ‘Slated’. (An amusing cameo.)<br /><br />Overall, I’d give this book 4 stars. The terminology really helps to immerse you in the world, even if I was confused to begin with. I felt very satisfied at the end of the book with where it finished and what had happened, everything just came together. Now I can’t wait to read the rest of Teri Terry’s works!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4090270633282708395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1155615772?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andie" href="/user/show/2703169-andie">Andie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2703169-andie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2703169-andie?shelf=sf">sf</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1155615772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1971409318328991852"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://toallthebooksivelovedbefore.wordpress.com/2015/02/07/mind-games-by-teri-terry/'>https://toallthebooksivelovedbefore.w...</a><br/><br/>Since I love the Slated trilogy so much, I was so excited to hear that Teri Terry has written a new book, a standalone. So of course I wanted to read it because it sounded mysterious and awesome.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, I didn’t love this book as much as I loved Slated, but Mind Games was still an interesting read.<br/><br/>I really liked Luna as a character because I could identify with her. She has lost her mother and had to live with a step-mother who wasn’t too fond of he</span>
  <span id="freeText1971409318328991852" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://toallthebooksivelovedbefore.wordpress.com/2015/02/07/mind-games-by-teri-terry/">https://toallthebooksivelovedbefore.w...</a><br /><br />Since I love the Slated trilogy so much, I was so excited to hear that Teri Terry has written a new book, a standalone. So of course I wanted to read it because it sounded mysterious and awesome.<br /><br />Unfortunately, I didn’t love this book as much as I loved Slated, but Mind Games was still an interesting read.<br /><br />I really liked Luna as a character because I could identify with her. She has lost her mother and had to live with a step-mother who wasn’t too fond of her and with an absent dad who rather prefered to spend most of his time in virtual worlds than with his family.<br /><br />I also liked her grandmother and I wish we could have learned more about her. Luna’s love interest was also very intriguing but I found the romance between Luna and Gecko rather innocent and I just felt that something was missing. I don’t know, I think the author could have concentrated more on the romance because it was barely there. I wanted to see more of these two together and that’s why I was a little disappointed.<br /><br />The world created by the author was however very fascinating, but also very complex and I often had troubles envisioning everything that happened in the virtual world. Still, I think that the whole idea of the book was very clever and also believable because technology could definitely be heading this way.<br /><br />The ending was scary and I didn’t expect it. Some disturbing secrets have been unveiled and what happened to some protagonists was really sad.<br /><br />All in all, Mind Games was an enjoyable read about a realistic and scary future and I think that this book will definitely appeal to sci-fi fans and those who enjoyed Teri Terry’s previous books.<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />3 out of 5 stars<br /><br />Note: I would like to thank Hachette Children’s Books for giving me the opportunity to review this book!<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14546430778516287602">The story takes place in a very interesting setting in the future. This future actually is not that unrealistic with this virtual reality and a manipulative superior organisation called PareCo. I think the author did a good job of creating the concept of this world. It was easy to imagine it inside my head.<br/><br/>The main character, however, was a bit questionable. She is a so - called refuser because she has this secret that she has to keep hidden. Besides, she always gets sick from logging on to the </span>
  <span id="freeText14546430778516287602" style="display:none">The story takes place in a very interesting setting in the future. This future actually is not that unrealistic with this virtual reality and a manipulative superior organisation called PareCo. I think the author did a good job of creating the concept of this world. It was easy to imagine it inside my head.<br /><br />The main character, however, was a bit questionable. She is a so - called refuser because she has this secret that she has to keep hidden. Besides, she always gets sick from logging on to the virtual reality (VR). And note: she's been that way for the majority of her 17 years on earth. <br />So one day she gets this hint to take some pills to avoid getting sick. She tries it and is completely excited about VR. I thought she avoided to log on to keep her secret. If she really wanted to find a way to avoid getting sick I'm sure she could have found the pills way earlier...<br /><br />Luna's behaviour is also really inconsistent in terms of her emotions, skills and intelligence. One second she's calm and talks reasonable, the next moment she's angry and dumb. Sometimes she has some spontaneous impressive skills, then completely incapable of understanding anything that people tell her.<br /><br />Suddenly she gets one of those implants that she refused to have for 17 years - and she doesn't even get angry for being compelled in such a deceitful way. Ah ok... <br />And after all she heard and experienced about PareCo she still simply thinks about "suing them". Ehm sure. I often wondered where her extraordinary "intelligence" and "rational" quotients were hiding. She didn't seem particularly bright to me. She just happened to have those special hacking skills bred into her DNA.<br /><br />So, this sounds quite negative. But apart from Luna, the story itself was really good :D<br />Well, except from the ending. It was a bit poor. Some people just die. Too bad - but hey! Luna found a fancy artist's name!!!</span>

<div id="review_1748815806" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1748815806" />
    <a title="H H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59315158-h-h"><img alt="H H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496196695p2/59315158.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1748815806?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="H H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="H H" href="/user/show/59315158-h-h">H H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1748815806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16908315352706325630">This book gave me wildly confusing feelings; some areas were covered well and some were questionable. The main character wasn't insanely boring. The premise of the book was good. It could have been amazing. . The idea of moving to the virtual world could have lead to intense combat scene and could have psychologically challenged the characters.<br/><br/>Instead though, the focus was once again- as in every book it seems- on a somewhat bland and forced lovestory. The first 2/5 of the book were good. The ch</span>
  <span id="freeText16908315352706325630" style="display:none">This book gave me wildly confusing feelings; some areas were covered well and some were questionable. The main character wasn't insanely boring. The premise of the book was good. It could have been amazing. . The idea of moving to the virtual world could have lead to intense combat scene and could have psychologically challenged the characters.<br /><br />Instead though, the focus was once again- as in every book it seems- on a somewhat bland and forced lovestory. The first 2/5 of the book were good. The characters were developing and the story seemed to be building up to a climax. But the introduction of the Gecko as a love interest..especially in a teen love story seemed....forced. That aspect seemed quite unrealistic.<br /><br />As the book progressed from this point it got gradually worse and worse. The plot decayed and characters that you thought would have more significance didn't (e.g. Sally, Melrose, Hex, Grandmother). Some parts of the book seemed rushed and too unrealistic; the romance, the resistance, but also how fast and easily the main character could develop skills. She was too good at everything. It seems like every time she got away with what she did was just because of chance, because she was the main character and she NEEDED to be good at something for the story. Some parts of the story seemed unneeded. This whole part (mid to end) was like it was written by a completely different person.<br /><br />The last 50 pages of the book seemed...wild. So much happened and so fast. The problem seemed too easy to "fix" though. The end of the book seemed somewhat rushed and unfinished. <br />Overall the book was mediocre. It built itself to be a better story than what it turned out to be, and in the end parts of the book seemed very forced. <br />It had potential though....<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16908315352706325630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1211305206" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1211305206" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1978609-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1233429155p2/1978609.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<span id="freeTextContainer16398288215184045875">I have always been a fan of Teri Terry and have met her on a couple of occasions and discovered she is also very nice to talk to. I heard she was coming to my local book store to do a talk and signing and as it was my Saturday off work I went. Sadly it wasn't very well attended but she still did her talk which was very interesting and discussed some of her books. I've only read the Slated series so far so was eager to know more. <br/><br/>I had this book on loan from the library (actually had been there f</span>
  <span id="freeText16398288215184045875" style="display:none">I have always been a fan of Teri Terry and have met her on a couple of occasions and discovered she is also very nice to talk to. I heard she was coming to my local book store to do a talk and signing and as it was my Saturday off work I went. Sadly it wasn't very well attended but she still did her talk which was very interesting and discussed some of her books. I've only read the Slated series so far so was eager to know more. <br /><br />I had this book on loan from the library (actually had been there for quite a while) and I hadn't got round to reading it but feeling inspired I picked it up and got stuck in. <br /><br />Luna knows she is different, everyone else spends most of their lives plugged into the virtual world, things are easier there. But Luna feels nauseous and can't settle to the technology. She then finds out a bigger secret behind the company and their technology but can she do anything before it's too late. <br /><br />I loved Luna, she was feisty and full of attitude but also inquisitive and caring. She seemed to trust a little too easily for my liking but then she had been quite sheltered growing up. I liked the development of the world and it was so well constructed that scarily enough you could actually see it happening with the advances in todays technology.<br /><br />I really liked Gecko and thought he was a great character and the mystery behinds Luna's mother was great.<br /><br />There is quite a lot of terminology and world building involved so you have to concentrate a bit but i just found it added to the world and it's experience.<br /><br />Really enjoyed it and definitely still a fan! Looking for the next book to read by Teri Terry now.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9668010678610874199">When I saw on NetGalley that I was going to read this book 4 months in advance, it was Christmas before Christmas. I am a huge fan of the Slated serie and I was expecting this book greatly.<br/><br/>We follow Luna, the world in which she lives is invaded by technology and the majority of people is connected to a virtual reality where they can meet, play, explore the seabed ... But Luna has the ability to see outside of this reality and to see the real world around her. It's a secret she must protect at al</span>
  <span id="freeText9668010678610874199" style="display:none">When I saw on NetGalley that I was going to read this book 4 months in advance, it was Christmas before Christmas. I am a huge fan of the Slated serie and I was expecting this book greatly.<br /><br />We follow Luna, the world in which she lives is invaded by technology and the majority of people is connected to a virtual reality where they can meet, play, explore the seabed ... But Luna has the ability to see outside of this reality and to see the real world around her. It's a secret she must protect at all costs, but things will change when she has to pass a fitness test and the danger will soon catch up.<br /><br />I must say that the theme of virtual realities, has often been used in books, but I was really surprised by the way of the story, it is far from video games and believe me the horror goes further, really further. I will not say much about the plot, but when you are going to read some of the revelations, you'll be shocked. I have again enjoyed the author's writing style, it is fluid, and easy reading.<br /><br />The only small thing that bothered me, I would say the end, the book takes its time to install the world, the threats and the plot and I found the end a bit rushed, there are a lot of stuffs and I have not always had time to assimilate them. Aside from that, this one-shot is really good, there is always a strong echo in our world and to the technological advance that sounds right. In short, a success for me.<br /><br />PS: I loved the Slated reference ^^</span>
  <a data-text-id="9668010678610874199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1134937462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12964081715959738584">Just the fact that it took me days to read this says lots.<br/><br/>Okay, the idea is pretty cool, I'll give the writer that. Though I have read Slated and know that I'm not dying to see more of her writing style, the blurb hinted a good subject, so I clicked that green button. While I don't regret it, not too much anyway, I could do without reading it.<br/><br/>At first, it felt like the plot was not going anywhere too interesting. We got our sc-fi world well described as promised, but every few pages, I found mys</span>
  <span id="freeText12964081715959738584" style="display:none">Just the fact that it took me days to read this says lots.<br /><br />Okay, the idea is pretty cool, I'll give the writer that. Though I have read Slated and know that I'm not dying to see more of her writing style, the blurb hinted a good subject, so I clicked that green button. While I don't regret it, not too much anyway, I could do without reading it.<br /><br />At first, it felt like the plot was not going anywhere too interesting. We got our sc-fi world well described as promised, but every few pages, I found myself stopping and thinking, "How would this even work?" and not being able to come up with an answer. Meaning, it simply didn't work for me. I wouldn't call it stupid, but almost.<br /><br />The characters were even worse. The only reason I didn't hate the MC is I was too indifferent to her, or the other characters including Jason, to actually feel something like hate. Once you don't feel anything towards the MC, the plot or the writing has to do a very good job to keep you reading. In this case, it doesn't.<br /><br />Also, the ending. Why would you rush something like that after taking your time to tell us more about your world? Are the plot or the characters less important than that? I was going to go wih a 3/5, but the ending got me way too disappointed to do that. Not sorry.<br /><br />Overall, a <b>2/5.</b> Not recommended.</span>

<div id="review_2297061930" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2297061930" />
    <a title="Ellesha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66449301-ellesha"><img alt="Ellesha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490914913p2/66449301.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2297061930?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellesha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellesha" href="/user/show/66449301-ellesha">Ellesha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66449301-ellesha?shelf=reviewed-books">reviewed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66449301-ellesha?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2297061930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11133456838678817221">I have mixed feelings about this book. I loved reading it and the concept of the book is amazing, with everyone being wrapped up in technology and it being so evolved that people don’t even need to live in the real world anymore. Definitely how I envision the world to be in years to come. However, I’m unsure on how to feel about how it ended, I can’t decide whether I like it or not, which is why it gets four stars instead of five. <br/><br/>The story itself was interesting, definitely different and extrem</span>
  <span id="freeText11133456838678817221" style="display:none">I have mixed feelings about this book. I loved reading it and the concept of the book is amazing, with everyone being wrapped up in technology and it being so evolved that people don’t even need to live in the real world anymore. Definitely how I envision the world to be in years to come. However, I’m unsure on how to feel about how it ended, I can’t decide whether I like it or not, which is why it gets four stars instead of five. <br /><br />The story itself was interesting, definitely different and extremely futuristic. I loved the main character, Luna and her journey of self discovery and saving the world was intense and fun to read. The description of everything throughout the book, such as the void and the virtual worlds created an amazing image in my head, making it such an enjoyable read. - I also loved the little nod to her Slated trilogy by making it one of the virtual worlds. <br /><br />The characters was all so different, there was a bit of everything from the strong, independent Luna, to the intelligent, cocky, but sensitive Gecko (who I loved), and of course, the mean girl Jezzamine. The mix of characters and Luna’s relationships with all of them is what I think gave the story emotion and purpose. <br /><br />The big twist is what did it for me, with finding out what’s on Inaccessible Island, it being almost a little sadistic but honest, like saying ‘this is what the human race will end up like’ with technology constantly developing - I loved this. However, this happened right towards the end of the book, so I felt that from then onwards, it was a little rushed which is why I am unsure on how I feel about the ending. I also don’t know how to feel about the very end of the book, how the story concludes and how things end with Luna. <br /><br />My favourite thing about this book was just the concept of it. The fact that people have an implant in them, and literally ‘plug in’ to machines to enter a virtual online world, I thought was amazing. I feel that Teri Terry has taken the idea of developing technology and has made the fact that everyone is always glued to their phones more literal with a dark tone, almost implying that with the rate of developing technology, in years to come, the human race will end up literally plugging in to access the internet. So much so, that it won’t be necessary for people to live in the real world anymore. - This alone, gave the book a high rating for me. Everything else including characters and storyline just added to that rating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11133456838678817221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1138378254" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1138378254" />
    <a title="Katy Noyes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6024557-katy-noyes"><img alt="Katy Noyes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447410722p2/6024557.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1138378254?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katy Noyes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katy Noyes" href="/user/show/6024557-katy-noyes">Katy Noyes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6024557-katy-noyes?shelf=netgalley-reviewcopy">netgalley-reviewcopy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1138378254" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15210095603822690502">4.5 stars<br/><br/>Terry really does have some great ideas. Slated was a fantastic concept, and different from it is Mind Games, though both find a basis in a technologically advanced world where human lives have been changed beyond recognition by software advances. I applaud the author her ideas, stunning.<br/><br/>And I raced through this. It's a good start when you can imagine the world of the characters in just a few pages, where the new technology and the associated vocabulary quickly becomes familiar to you a</span>
  <span id="freeText15210095603822690502" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />Terry really does have some great ideas. Slated was a fantastic concept, and different from it is Mind Games, though both find a basis in a technologically advanced world where human lives have been changed beyond recognition by software advances. I applaud the author her ideas, stunning.<br /><br />And I raced through this. It's a good start when you can imagine the world of the characters in just a few pages, where the new technology and the associated vocabulary quickly becomes familiar to you as a reader. Luna's world grew for me into a fully-functioning one instantly. In Luna's world, everyone (or almost everyone) has an Implant. Implants allow humans to experience a shared virtual world, one that is now so standard that refusers like Luna are in a tiny minority. Luna has her reasons for refusing, but finds it increasingly difficult to continue when she is unexpectedly sent for tests that will admit her to the highest-level universities and job pools when she graduates. She does know the virtual world, she's been there, but unlike other people she can't switch off awareness of her body while inside it. Nobody knows of her ability though, and she must try hard to keep it a secret, which will be tricky when the tests begin in earnest...<br /><br />That only kicks off the story though, we have a Matrix-like world where Luna and her fellow students function in the real world and become quite different in the virtual one. It's very well written, to create the world in the mind of the reader. I actually did want to visit the Grid of Luna's virtual world. I certainly want to see the film of this!<br /><br />Other characters feature through the story, though I had hopes for one that plot-wise has to disappear for a huge chunk of the book - missed him. There is an underlying question throughout about how much we should invest ourselves in virtual worlds and ignore or give secondary consideration to what's happening in the REAL world. Luna's father works in the virtual world, emerging rarely to see his family. Her little brother will probably end up being schooled almost wholly there, as the schools in the real world are starting to close through lack of students walking through their doors. It did make me consider what I think about this kind of technology.<br /><br />But as thriller / adventure / fantasy young adult reads go, it's a fast-paced and exciting read. I do admit, I lost track of what was happening a few times near the end, it moved too quickly for me to understand exactly what was happening at times, and did wrap up very fast at the climax. But I thoroughly enjoyed my own mind's journey into Luna's virtual world.<br /><br />Recommended if you're a fan of dystopia-set fiction, technological/fantasy stories or fast-paced YA reads.<br /><br />Review of a Netgalley advance copy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15210095603822690502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1128407010" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1128407010" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1128407010?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan  (thebookishtwins)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan  (thebookishtwins)" href="/user/show/12484735-megan-thebookishtwins">Megan  (thebookishtwins)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12484735-megan-thebookishtwins?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12484735-megan-thebookishtwins?shelf=not-in-usa-or-american-protaganist">not-in-usa-or-american-protaganist</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12484735-megan-thebookishtwins?shelf=ukya">ukya</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1128407010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11485583261156961080"><i>I received this free from the publishers via NetGalley</i><br/><br/><b>DNF - 40%</b><br/><br/>Luna is a Refuser because she has trouble fully existing in the virtual world because part of her is still in the real world. Luna tries to cover this up and to keep her secret. She has trouble keeping her secret when she is selected for testing. However, Luna starts to hope of a better future, and that can be dangerous. <br/><br/>I requested this purely due to the author, <i>Teri Terry</i> as I really enjoyed <i>Slated</i>. However <i>Mind Games</i> just did not </span>
  <span id="freeText11485583261156961080" style="display:none"><i>I received this free from the publishers via NetGalley</i><br /><br /><b>DNF - 40%</b><br /><br />Luna is a Refuser because she has trouble fully existing in the virtual world because part of her is still in the real world. Luna tries to cover this up and to keep her secret. She has trouble keeping her secret when she is selected for testing. However, Luna starts to hope of a better future, and that can be dangerous. <br /><br />I requested this purely due to the author, <i>Teri Terry</i> as I really enjoyed <i>Slated</i>. However <i>Mind Games</i> just did not capture my attention at all, and left me unsatisfied, hence the DNF. While I can't recommend it or dissuade anyone from reading this book because I haven't finished it, I'll still review what I read. <br /><br />In terms of world building, I was not that impressed. I did not really get a sense of this <i>virtual world</i> and I felt like it was not explained or shown as much as it could have been. How did they enter the virtual world? So there were questions which weren't answered in the first half, and it really affected my enjoyment because I could not fully dive into the world and dystopian society. I also felt like, in terms of world building, some background information might have been useful, for example, how did the world end up like that, using virtual technology? Also, I'm really not that tech savvy, so a whole book and plot based around technology and virtual worlds just confused me and did not interest me. To be fair, those who enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16279856.The_Eye_of_Minds__The_Mortality_Doctrine___1_" title="The Eye of Minds (The Mortality Doctrine, #1) by James Dashner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Eye of Minds</a> by James Dashner would probably enjoy this one, as they have some similar aspects, however, James Dashner does explain the connection between the body in the real world and the virtual world better than Teri Terry. <br /><br />In terms of the characters, I personally did not think they were very fleshed out at all and had a hard time connecting with any of them. They felt quite two-dimensional and I did not really feel any of the bonds between the characters. Especially between Luna and Gecko as I felt their dialogue was stilted and forced and it just felt a bit awkward to me. <br /><br />Overall, I felt like it lacked world building and depth to the characters. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11485583261156961080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1200662515" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1200662515" />
    <a title="Claire (Book Blog Bird)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10982678-claire-book-blog-bird"><img alt="Claire (Book Blog Bird)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343948552p2/10982678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1200662515?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claire (Book Blog Bird)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claire (Book Blog Bird)" href="/user/show/10982678-claire-book-blog-bird">Claire (Book Blog Bird)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10982678-claire-book-blog-bird?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10982678-claire-book-blog-bird?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10982678-claire-book-blog-bird?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1200662515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15787843575874220356">I was given a copy of Mind Games in exchange for an honest review. Many thanks to Hachette and Netgalley.<br/><br/>A copy of this review is also on my blog: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.bookblogbird.weebly.com'>www.bookblogbird.weebly.com</a><br/><br/>Mind Games is set in the near future and tells the story of Luna, one of the few people who are unable to access the virtual world offered by PareCo (Woop! Woop! Evil Corporation Alert!) that the rest of the population spend their education and leisure time in.<br/><br/>Thinking that her future will be limited to the dead-end jobs off</span>
  <span id="freeText15787843575874220356" style="display:none">I was given a copy of Mind Games in exchange for an honest review. Many thanks to Hachette and Netgalley.<br /><br />A copy of this review is also on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookblogbird.weebly.com">www.bookblogbird.weebly.com</a><br /><br />Mind Games is set in the near future and tells the story of Luna, one of the few people who are unable to access the virtual world offered by PareCo (Woop! Woop! Evil Corporation Alert!) that the rest of the population spend their education and leisure time in.<br /><br />Thinking that her future will be limited to the dead-end jobs offered to those who refuse virtual life, everyone is astonished when Luna is offered a space in the PareCo tests which will give her the opportunity of an amazing future at university or even at PareCo’s Think Tanks, developing new virtual worlds. When she arrives it’s the start of a huge voyage of self-discovery.<br /><br />I thought Mind Games was an all-round good book, with some aspects that were just excellent. The baddies have their evil lair in a hollowed-out volcano and I don’t care which way you turn it: baddies in hollowed-out volcanoes are awesome. The characters are ace and you really end up caring about them. Luna was a super protagonist and it’s really interesting to read all the different ways her friends and family use virtual worlds.<br /><br />The world has been built with a lot of thought to detail. It’s very recognisable and scarily believable as a future London where people just spend all their time in virtual reality. Teri Terry hasn’t made PareCo too crazy-evil and that just makes them all the more creepy and sinister.<br /><br />I felt the pace of the story slowed down a bit in the middle after a nice, action-y start and the end felt a tiny bit rushed, but this wasn’t enough to put me off and I was glad it didn’t because the finale is electric with a couple of truly ‘No-o-o-o-o-o!’ moments.<br /><br />I was really looking forward to Mind Games, and I have to say it didn’t disappoint.<br />Recommended for: anyone who likes techno-future dystopias and The Matrix.<br /><br />8.5/10<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15787843575874220356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
